Current Affairs Commentary

Britain in the International Crisis 42

— Corner

What Hitler, Mussolini, and the Japanese authorities are hoping for has long been revealed by their own words and actions. Countries that have been invaded or are at risk of invasion should form a united front, retaliating in kind: an eye for an eye, using anti-aircraft guns against aircraft, and gas masks against poisonous gas. This is undoubtedly the most appropriate and intelligent approach. However, establishing a common front for peace is easier said than done. For example, Britain has the power to influence the global political landscape, but the British Conservative Party, despite knowing that the formation of an aggressive front would endanger world peace, still clings to outdated foreign policies without changing. Although British Foreign Secretary Eden made a solemn speech at the International Chamber of Commerce on the first of this month, stating that "If Belgium is invaded by another country without provocation, Britain will come to its aid," as if he were very concerned about events on the continent, the reality is quite different. German diplomats have seen through Britain's true intentions and understand the shortsightedness of the British Conservatives. As long as Germany does not infringe on British interests, Britain is happy to turn a blind eye to Germany's free actions. Therefore, after the announcement of the German-Japanese agreement, Germany immediately telegraphed the British government to reassure them, saying, "The German-Japanese agreement contains no secret clauses." And the "Morning Post," the mouthpiece of the British Conservative Party, also said, "The German-Japanese agreement is nothing shocking. In a word, it is nothing more than mutual cooperation to curb the malicious activities of the Communist International." With a few dismissive words, the crimes of the aggressors are brushed aside. Such an attitude can be described as the Conservatives having a tendency towards seeking kindred spirits, or as focusing only on short-term survival without any long-term vision.

We know that the Conservative Party's sole aim is not to eliminate war, but to keep Britain from being drawn into it. Former Prime Minister MacDonald, a quasi-Conservative New Labour bureaucrat, once stated, "Maintaining the Eastern European status quo is not our immediate concern. What we must guard against is being drawn into a war caused by a combination of France and Germany's eastern neighbor (referring to the Soviet Union)." These words reveal the entire picture of Conservative diplomacy without missing a single detail. On the first of this month, Foreign Secretary Eden's opinion on the German-Japanese agreement in the House of Commons stated that "Britain's attitude towards the agreement is to oppose the trend of dividing the world into several blocs, especially for ideological reasons. British policy still aims to promote friendship between all countries." This is also a concrete explanation of their defeatist attitude.

Because Britain wants to avoid being drawn into the whirlpool of war and because it wants to promote so-called friendship between all countries, what it hopes for is only regional security in Western Europe. If Germany can comply with Britain's desire and guarantee Belgium's neutrality, the Conservative Party will already feel satisfied. Germany's various actions that violate treaties can be ignored and not questioned. This is Britain's attitude towards Germany. As for another ambitious country that has recently risen in the Mediterranean - Italy - its nouveau riche demeanor has already made the British uneasy during the Italian-Abyssinian War. However, under the major premise of not hindering British interests and at the same time allowing Britain to avoid being drawn into war, there is still room for compromise between Britain and Italy. We have also seen a gentlemen's agreement on Mediterranean issues put forward between London and Rome.

Although Britain is still clearly wandering on the political road today, the evolution of world affairs will always make Britain realize that it must make a decision. The renowned scholar Laski recently said, "The conflicts of capitalism are aggressive wars. This fact is clearly contained in the policies of the fascist powers. It is a delusion to think that we (referring to the British) can stay out of the war. The only way to prevent war is to unite with those powerful countries that have no aggressive ambitions and give the fascist powers a warning: that if they want to change borders by force, they will have to contend with the force of us and our allied countries." We believe that these words can not only serve as medicine for the British Conservatives but can also serve as a motto for the people of countries that are being invaded.

Roosevelt Arrives in Uruguay, Receives a Grand Welcome 43

Montevideo—U.S. President Roosevelt arrived here today from Buenos Aires, Argentina, and received a grand welcome. The President of Uruguay personally led senior government officials to the port to greet him. (Reuter, 3rd)

Montevideo—U.S. President Roosevelt, aboard the cruiser USS Indianapolis, arrived here from Buenos Aires at 8:50 this morning. Uruguayan President Terra led cabinet members and diplomatic corps personnel to the docks to greet him. Several squadrons of aircraft flew in the sky over the harbor to show their welcome. After landing, President Roosevelt toured the city. (Havas, 3rd)

Buenos Aires—U.S. President Roosevelt departed from here today aboard the cruiser USS Indianapolis to return to the United States. Before departing, he hosted a banquet for Argentine President Justo and his wife, and declared upon boarding the ship that the U.S. Good Neighbor policy could be applied to the commercial and political relations of all American countries. The President will arrive in Montevideo at 9:30 tonight and stay for several hours. (Reuter, 3rd)

German Diet Movement 44

(Berlin) In view of the complexity of German restaurant menus, the Restaurant Association yesterday sent a letter to its members asking them to reduce the number of dishes. The letter pointed out that the more dishes there are, the greater the consumption. During this time of national thrift, simple menus should be emphasized. The King's Marriage Causes a Huge Uproar; A Major Constitutional Dispute in British History; The Cabinet Anxiously Issues its First Declaration; Newspapers Deeply Fear that the Imperial System is Weakening 45

(London) Edward VIII's relationship with Mrs. Simpson and the Cabinet's attitude towards this matter are still at an impasse. (London) The rumors about the King's marriage to American woman Mrs. Simpson have been circulating for weeks. The Emperor's Marriage is Not Free; Causing a City-Wide Sensation; The Prime Minister and Bishops Repeatedly Advise; Will the King Marry Mrs. Simpson with the Title of Duke of Cornwall? 46

(London) King Edward's dispute with the Cabinet over his desire to marry Mrs. Simpson has made Prime Minister Baldwin possibly on the verge of resigning. Baldwin once again met with Edward today. According to reports from courtiers at Buckingham Palace, the Prime Minister asked Edward to decide on his future relationship with Mrs. Simpson within 48 hours, otherwise, Parliament would take "tough measures." It is learned that before the Prime Minister's audience, the Cabinet held a meeting and decided on a compromise solution, allowing Edward to marry Mrs. Simpson, but Mrs. Simpson could only use the title of Duchess of Cornwall. Baldwin presented this proposal to Edward, and Edward replied, "Then who is the King?" Therefore, rumors spread that Baldwin was about to resign. Newspapers here today all published editorials criticizing the King in the strongest language ever, mostly supporting the Prime Minister and wanting to prevent Mrs. Simpson from becoming Queen of England. However, most commentators also believe that the King can respect his responsibilities to the country and abandon his relationship with Mrs. Simpson. The "News Chronicle" reported that the Bishop of Bradford's speech yesterday had indicated that a major constitutional dispute had arisen between the King and the Cabinet. The problem is: "Whether Mrs. Simpson is qualified to become Queen, and whether this matter should be decided by the King or the Cabinet are all questions, but the answer to the question is not difficult. Who should be a lifelong companion? The monarch of a country is also an ordinary person and should have the right to decide for himself. Or should the Queen be determined by Parliament? If the King has the right to decide, then what is the conflict with the Cabinet's so-called constitutional problem? Moreover, the British throne is a hereditary presidential system and does not have a divine nature, so the general public may be happy to see their monarch marry the one he loves. However, there is no shortage of women who oppose divorce and American women becoming queens." If Edward insists on marrying Mrs. Simpson, the public may wish him to use the title of Duke of Cornwall. In this way, all disputes can be avoided. The "Cavalry" magazine will announce the "inside story" of this cabinet crisis tomorrow. It is said that the Prime Minister met with the King on November 25 to discuss the economic problems of South Wales. At that time, he also touched on the King's marriage issue. The Prime Minister said, "I have received strong notices from Australia, Canada, and South Africa. If Your Majesty marries Mrs. Simpson, the British Empire will be in danger of disintegration." Edward then asked the Prime Minister who was the King of England. Afterwards, Baldwin discussed with Lord Halifax, the Lord Privy Seal, Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain, Leader of the House of Lords Earl Peel, and newspaper leader Lord Beaverbrook. A special Cabinet meeting was convened again last Friday. Now, the King has apparently decided to marry Mrs. Simpson and will force the Cabinet to obey, without abdicating. People close to the palace said that the King would meet with Mrs. Simpson today to decide on the course of action to be taken. The labor insurance company has also raised the premium for delaying the King's coronation until the end of next year, which is also very meaningful. (Reuter, 3rd)

(London) Some people advocate that the King's spouse does not have to be honored as Queen. If this statement becomes a reality, it will cause serious difficulties, especially the attitude of the self-governing regions towards Britain, which will be the most troublesome. The British self-governing territories are already independent in the constitution, and their only link with the mother country is the King and Queen. Therefore, a monarch marrying a commoner is unprecedented in history. The prestige of the royal family will inevitably suffer a blow, and the link between the mother country and the self-governing territories will be dissolved accordingly. Observers recently pointed this out solemnly, and representatives of the self-governing territories have also repeatedly stated this. (Havas, 3rd)

(London) According to responsible sources, Prime Minister Baldwin has proposed to the House of Commons to temporarily change today's afternoon agenda. Political figures believe that the House of Commons is taking this procedure to discuss a very important issue, which must be related to the marriage of King Edward VIII and Mrs. Simpson. Although the Cabinet did not convene a meeting today, the cabinet members continued to discuss incessantly at the Prime Minister's official residence at 10 Downing Street. The Prime Minister first talked with the Lord Privy Seal Halifax for a long time, and then decided to talk with Liberal Party leader Sinclair and Home Secretary Simon. However, responsible sources believe that the Cabinet will never resign, because the Cabinet members believe that the King's marriage is purely a constitutional issue. (Agence Havas, 3rd)

(London) According to reliable sources, the King resolutely refused today to wear an army uniform at the coronation ceremony. (Reuter, 3rd)

Newspapers That Have Kept Silent Now Suddenly Discuss; A Bishop's Word Breaks the Silence; American Newspapers Report More and More Extravagantly 47

(London) After Bishop Welch read the newspapers' criticisms of his speech, he told a Reuters reporter, "The actions of these people have exceeded the rights they should have. Only one sentence in my speech can be regarded as a criticism of the British Emperor. What I said, 'England needs God's grace,' is because the British Emperor seems to regard all religious conventions as insignificant on the surface, which is quite regrettable. My speech was drafted six weeks before I first heard the various rumors, so the wording in it has absolutely nothing to do with the rumors. I have been very careful to avoid mentioning the British Emperor's private life, because I don't know much about it." (Reuters, 3rd)

(London) British newspapers, which have kept silent about the rumors that King Edward intends to marry American woman Mrs. Simpson as his queen, have now finally been broken by the major newspapers across the country. Some newspapers spoke frankly, while others were still implicit. According to the "Daily Mail" and the "Daily Express," the matter has now reached the point of constitutional conflict, because the Emperor has expressed his intention to marry against the advice of the Cabinet. The "News Chronicle" is the only newspaper that mentioned Mrs. Simpson's name, saying that the point of contention now is whether this woman is suitable to be the Queen of England, and whether this matter will be decided by the Emperor himself or by the government representing public opinion. The "Daily Mail" also mentioned the possibility of abdication, saying that "this move will make the Emperor's loyal subjects feel extremely sad." The "Daily Mail" announced in the news column this morning that the Emperor had refused to accept the advice of ministers on matters involving his private life. Last night, Prime Minister Baldwin told the Emperor that the Cabinet was deeply concerned about the Emperor's rumored marriage plans. At a time when international affairs are in crisis, the Emperor's actions will hinder the interests of the country and the Empire. The matter is of great importance, and the cabinet members sold their advice, begging the Emperor to pay special attention to the news from several self-governing territories, which has frankly stated the attitude of their governments towards the Emperor's actions. The "Daily Mail" also learned that the Prime Minister had expressed his deep regret on behalf of the entire Cabinet, saying that the cabinet members had decided that unless an agreement could be reached, there would inevitably be a cabinet crisis and a constitutional dispute. The Cabinet believes that the best policy is for the Emperor to announce to the country that he does not want to complete this marriage.

(London) "The Times" today published an editorial entitled "The Emperor and the Monarch," which stated briefly that Bishop Bradford's famous speech had aroused a lot of criticism from newspapers in northern England, not only in Leeds and Bradford, but also in Manchester, Nottingham, Darlington, and Birmingham.

It is heard that the criticisms from the above-mentioned famous newspapers in various places are mostly based on the arguments of the two bishops. Although one or two newspapers hinted that if the Emperor's intention conflicts with the loyal advice of cabinet members, it will cause a serious constitutional dispute, most of them believe that the true value of Bishop Bradford's speech can be seen in the various declarations published in major American newspapers and some self-governing territory newspapers. We should not ignore it.

The newspaper continued, saying that Britain has always paid little attention to American propaganda, but now the American newspapers are becoming more and more extravagant, and their propaganda materials have involved the Emperor's private life.

The newspaper continued, saying that the duties of the king have never been easy, especially for a king who is middle-aged and has not yet enjoyed a happy marriage. According to general speculation, it is often thought that the Emperor's current age should be more tolerant and magnanimous than his previous emperors, and there is a feeling that the throne must be placed above public criticism. The Emperor himself should also enjoy the right to enjoy comfort and choose friends as companions. However, there is one thing that he and the whole country must consider: if his personal tendencies and public responsibilities often conflict, then the power of his high position will inevitably weaken day by day.

As far as the current events are concerned, the hidden dangers and dangers are self-evident. The rumors and gossip on the other side of the Atlantic have spread extremely rapidly and are no longer limited to the small scope related to the United States. As for the British newspapers, which have not seen any criticisms so far, it is only due to ordinary self-esteem and the hope that the Emperor can have an authoritative action or a formal declaration so that all rumors and gossips can be completely eliminated from the invisible. At present, such action or declaration is extremely needed, because if various rumors are allowed to exist for a long time, the result will inevitably seriously affect our country. The high position occupied by the Emperor is a sacred trust, because the whole nation's willingness to be loyal makes its maintenance power increase day by day.

The above-mentioned events are more important today than at any time in history. There are two reasons: first, due to the development of constitutional government in the British Empire, the responsibilities borne by the Emperor are far heavier than in the past, and the public opinion of the people in the various self-governing territories has now automatically shifted to the monarch, and regards him as the only link with the motherland. Second, due to the seriousness of the world situation, the duties of the British monarch are becoming more and more important, because he must be the mainstay in the midst of the communist and fascist tides. The situation was like this a year ago, and we hope that the situation will remain the same after the Emperor's official coronation within the next year. However, the public needs a concrete guarantee to know that this mainstay has not been shaken. (Reuters, 3rd)

Spanish Rebel Army Launches New Land and Air Assaults on Capital; Government Forces Fight Valiantly, Refusing to Retreat; Casualties on Both Sides Reach Approximately Three Thousand 51

Madrid - Rebel forces resumed their attack on the capital today from both the air and the ground. Twenty-four high-speed rebel destroyers provided cover as seven bombers first bombed the northwestern district of the capital twice. A large contingent of infantry immediately followed with a fierce attack, and fierce fighting is currently underway. (3rd National Telegram)

Madrid - Yesterday's rebel offensive was the fiercest since the siege of the capital began. Currently, the fighting is most intense around the village of Pozuelo to the west of the capital. The village has been reduced to ruins as a result of heavy artillery bombardment and three air raids. However, as of this afternoon, the militia continues to defend the village to the death, refusing to retreat. (3rd Reuters Telegram)

Madrid - Twenty-four rebel aircraft attacked the capital twice today, dropping no fewer than forty bombs on the western suburban university district. The defending forces' anti-aircraft guns fired at them, but to no effect. Today's "Social News" estimates that since the rebel siege of the capital began, the total number of rebel casualties has reached 11,000. (2nd National Telegram)

Seven Giant German Aircraft Arrive in Morocco to Resupply Rebel Forces; Use of Green Gas by Rebels Confirmed; British MP Asks for Gas Masks to be Sent Home; Belgian Communist Party's Recruitment of Volunteers Raided 52

Tangier - Yesterday, seven giant, three-engine German aircraft landed in Tetouan, Spanish Morocco. (2nd Havas Telegram)

(London) According to news received here today, the German Army Headquarters is currently recruiting volunteers to join the Nationalist tank corps in Spain. (2nd National News Agency Telegram)

Madrid - After inspecting the civil war here, a delegation from the British Parliament cabled the British House of Commons, saying, "There is an urgent need for gas masks in the city of Madrid. Please purchase and send them here for use as quickly as possible to the greatest extent possible. We would be most grateful." In addition, a cable was sent to General Franco, the Nationalist government leader, stating, "The city of Madrid was again brutally bombed this morning, resulting in casualties among women and children. We strongly condemn and protest the Nationalist forces' aircraft bombing of civilian residential areas." (3rd Havas Telegram)

Madrid - Nationalist aircraft previously dropped bombs containing poisonous gas in the capital, resulting in the injury and death of ten government soldiers due to poisoning. Dr. Frankel, a medical officer in the international brigade composed of left-wing volunteers from various countries, recently stated that the gas is called "Green Cross Gas." In addition, a government soldier who served in the military during the European War recently stated that he was poisoned twice while fighting in Belgium. He knows that those poisoned by this type of gas will suffer severe damage to their brain nerves, profuse cold sweat on their face, and suffocation. (3rd Havas Telegram)

Brussels - Because the Communist Party is recruiting volunteers to go to Spain to aid the Popular Front government, the police conducted searches of the party's offices throughout the country yesterday. Thirty offices were searched in the city of Liège and seventeen in Charleroi. It was discovered that the organization for recruitment was very well-established. Recruiting personnel were assigned to various cities and towns. Those who volunteered to join the army were registered, and lists were compiled and sent to the capital. The volunteers were formed into squads, escorted to the border, and given train tickets and travel expenses to travel to Spain. (3rd Havas Telegram)

Brussels - The police were ordered yesterday to search the Communist Party headquarters throughout the country. It is now known that this action was initiated because the military authorities repeatedly reported that there had been many desertions from the Belgian army recently, some going to Madrid, the capital of Spain, and others joining the Nationalist forces there. Therefore, yesterday's search was not limited to Communist Party offices; the offices of right-wing National Volunteers were also searched. It was discovered that both sides of the Spanish civil war had sent personnel to actively operate within Belgium. Xu Lutai, a former official at the Spanish embassy in Belgium, is one notable example. (3rd Havas Telegram)

A Village's Gain or Loss Still Worth Fighting For; Government Forces Speak Many Languages 53

Madrid - Fierce fighting occurred yesterday between the university hospital and the Forlask Institute in the northwestern suburbs of the city. The village of Delapo there is where the Nationalist forces were entrenched. The objective of the government forces was to retake this village. A team of hand grenade soldiers belonging to the Asturias militia, along with the International Brigade, was dispatched to attack. The enemy in the village suddenly responded with tanks. The militia immediately stopped advancing. When the tanks approached, they bravely charged and destroyed them with hand grenades. They then took advantage of the victory to advance and occupy the village of Delapo. All the soldiers, each speaking their own language, sang the Internationale with great fervor. (3rd Havas Agency Telegram)

Belgian House of Representatives Passes Military Buildup Plan; Military Service Extended to Eighteen Months; Honoring Anglo-Franco-Belgian Military Cooperation 54

Brussels - The House of Representatives recently passed the army reform bill by a vote of 137 to 43, with only eight members abstaining. The Flemish Nationalists, Communists, and a small number of Socialists voted against it. All members of the Fascist Rex Party voted in favor. The main points of this bill are four: (1) Extend the term of military service: for infantry, from twelve months to eighteen months, and for other types of soldiers, from eight months to twelve months; (2) Strengthen defensive fortifications; (3) Adopt various measures to enable rapid mobilization in the event of an emergency; (4) Recruit 6,000 volunteers. (3rd Havas Telegram)

Brussels - Prime Minister Zélande delivered a speech explaining the reasons for extending the term of military service, saying that the tense situation in Europe is unprecedented since 1914. In order to protect Belgium's security, it is necessary to extend the term of military service. Zélande went on to mention King Leopold III's speech on October 14, regarding Belgium's policy of neutrality, saying that there were two motivations for this speech: one was Germany's re-establishment of defenses along the Rhine River, and the other was the weakening of the League of Nations. Belgium is determined to participate in negotiations on the Western European Pact to promote its success, but Belgium will not renew any agreement that would hinder its policy of independence. "We will certainly honor the agreement reached by the Anglo-Franco-Belgian general staffs in London in July of this year, but this agreement is only temporary in nature. I hope that the future Western European Pact will be established quickly. As for the guarantees that our country provided to France, Britain, and Germany in 1925, they were necessary at the time, but they are no longer effective. Therefore, we cannot provide the same guarantees to those countries at this time. In short, our main responsibility is only to prevent our country from becoming a base for war." (2nd Havas Telegram)

(London) When the House of Commons met today, Liberal MP Mond raised a question to Foreign Secretary Eden, saying that if France were to be invaded because it fulfilled the Franco-Russian Mutual Assistance Pact, or because it fulfilled its alliances with the Little Entente and Poland, would Britain also have an obligation to assist France and Belgium? Eden replied, "Britain's obligations to France and Belgium are based on the Locarno Treaty. This is clearly stipulated in the treaty and there is no doubt. Britain expects that the British obligations contained in future treaties will be consistent with those stipulated in the Locarno Treaty." (2nd Havas Telegram)

Serious Labor Unrest Among US Seamen; Strikers Clash with Police 56

(New York) Today, police clashed with 750 striking workers at the New York docks, resulting in eight arrests and several injuries. At the same time, disputes have arisen within the International Labor Union, which was formed in connection with the dockworkers' strike. The French mail steamer "Chambellan," which arrived here today, was unable to unload 600 tons of cargo. Dockworkers in Cherbourg, France, recently refused to unload cargo from the Washington mail steamer to show solidarity with the American seamen's strike. However, this strike has not been recognized by the New York French Dockworkers' Union. In retaliation, the New York dockworkers refused to unload the cargo carried by the "Chambellan," except for mail and perishable goods. Therefore, the ship had to return to Europe with its original cargo. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

France Expands Naval Preparations; Aircraft Increase to 1,500; Warship Construction Program to be Completed in Four and a Half Years 59

(Paris) Minister of Aviation Cot recently presented a report on the strength of the Air Force to the Finance Committee of the House of Representatives, expressing optimism and stating that the French Air Force has been completely reformed and reorganized in the past three years. Once the plan to nationalize the military aircraft manufacturing industry is implemented, the aircraft manufacturing plants will be distributed throughout the country instead of being concentrated in one area. The work of reforming the Air Force will also be further advanced. As for the aircraft construction plan, the original target for the 1937 fiscal year was 1,085 aircraft, but it has now been decided to add 415 aircraft, for a total of 1,500 aircraft. (2nd Havas Telegram)

(Paris) Minister of Maritime Affairs Gaspard declared to the Naval Committee of the House of Representatives today the degree to which the French navy will be strengthened. Gaspard declared that by 1943 France will have five battleships of 35,000 tons each, ten cruisers of 10,000 tons each, for a total of 275,000 tons. It is estimated that this expenditure will require 2,500,000,000 francs and will be completed in four and a half years. According to Admiral Dubark, who recently declared to the Finance Committee of the House of Representatives, the tonnage of the French naval fleet is not comparable to the naval fleets of its neighboring countries, so Gaspard made this statement today. At the same time, Kandas, the naval budget reporter, declared that the major powers are building warships on a large scale in a very short period of time, while France is still implementing its naval construction program in accordance with the clauses in the Treaty of Versailles. France will soon be downgraded from fourth to sixth place among the naval powers. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

Saint-Nazaire Port - The new battleship "Strasbourg" has now been completed and is scheduled to be launched here on the 12th of this month. The ship has a displacement of 26,500 tons, a length of 215 meters, and a speed of 29.5 knots per hour. (2nd Havas Telegram)

France Plans to Establish Air Route Across North Atlantic 61

(Paris) Minister of Aviation Cot declared to the Aviation Committee of the House of Representatives today that the air service between France and the United States across the Atlantic is currently being planned. It will require an expenditure of 60 million francs. It has been discussed to organize a company representing Air France, the French Postal Company, and the State. The State will hold the majority of the shares. An international agreement will also be established to avoid conflicts between this service and the services of other countries. Mail may be transported next year or the year after. Two routes are currently being surveyed: one is the route through the Azores, and the other is the route through Saint Pierre Island off the coast of Newfoundland. The former route is being surveyed by the famous transatlantic pilot, Codus, and the latter route is being surveyed by Captain Foxiller. Seaplane bases will be established in both locations. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

Philippine Hurricane 62

(Manila) According to reports received by the local weather bureau, a hurricane occurred today in Naga, Camarines Sur province. Traffic in the area has been disrupted, so the extent of the damage cannot be ascertained. The local area is waiting for the arrival of the typhoon today. It is currently raining heavily, and water is accumulating in the streets. There have been many reports of wind damage to trees and roofs. Shipping has been suspended, and small boats have entered the harbor to take shelter from the wind. Giant waves are pounding the dikes along the beach. The US Asiatic Fleet has sailed out of the harbor. It is now known that the hurricane passed over Atimonan, 100 miles southeast of Manila, at 3:00 AM this morning and is currently moving slowly towards the area. The weather bureau stated that the hurricane's center is moving at a speed of 60 miles per hour, with a pressure of 11 pounds per square foot. (3rd National Telegram)

Australian-Japanese Trade Agreement Reached 63

(Tokyo) Australian-Japanese trade negotiations: Consul-General Murai met with a representative of the Australian Parliament and reached a compromise. Concrete measures are currently being worked out. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs consulted with related parties on the 2nd on the issue of canceling the invocation of the Trade Protection Act. Today, a compromise method was decided. The Japanese and Australian governments will each declare the cancellation of the reduction of high tariff input evaluation systems and the invocation of the Trade Protection Act as the first step. As for the second step of negotiating the abolition of the treaty, it will begin after the arrival of the new Consul-General, Lao Song. (3rd Allied Telegram)

Rigorous Implementation of Household Registration and Baojia System in Chahar Province; Public Security Bureau Formulates Provisional Measures to Prevent Petty Thieves and Strictly Suppress Disturbances 67

Zhangjiakou Correspondence: The Public Security Bureau of Chahar Provincial Capital, in order to maintain public order, strengthen public organization, thoroughly investigate household registration to prevent petty thieves from lurking and taking advantage of opportunities to create disturbances, and to ensure that officials and civilians are integrated without separation, and to handle matters quickly and efficiently, has formulated the "Provisional Measures for Compiling and Investigating Baojia and Household Registration under the Jurisdiction of the Chahar Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau" based on the "Regulations on Compiling and Investigating Baojia and Household Registration in Counties of Bandit Suppression Areas" promulgated by the Military Commission, and submitted it to the provincial government for implementation. It is now being actively implemented. The measures are recorded below:

(1) The Bureau formulates these measures specifically to maintain the security of the provincial capital, strengthen public organization, thoroughly investigate household registration to prevent petty thieves from lurking and taking advantage of opportunities to create disturbances, seek integration of officials and civilians, avoid separation, and handle matters quickly. It is based on the "Regulations on Compiling and Investigating Baojia and Household Registration in Counties of Bandit Suppression Areas" promulgated by the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government in July of the 24th year of the Republic of China. (2) The Baojia areas of Chahar Provincial Capital are divided into five districts according to the police districts of each Public Security Sub-bureau. Each district has a district head, concurrently held by the sub-bureau chief. The five districts are divided into twenty-nine towns, with six towns in the first district, six towns in the second district, eight towns in the third district, six towns in the fourth district, and three towns in the fifth district. Each town has a town head. The household registration within the town is based on the household as a unit, with a household head. Ten households form a Jia, with a Jia head. Ten Jia form a Bao, with a Bao head. The election of the town, Bao, and Jia heads is done as follows: the Jia head is publicly elected by the household heads within the Jia, the Bao head is publicly elected by the Jia heads within the Bao, and the town head is publicly elected by the Bao heads within the town. (The town head can also serve as Bao head, and the Bao head can also serve as Jia head.) However, a meeting of the sub-bureau chiefs and stationed patrol officers must be convened in advance to not only divide the areas of each town, but also instruct the stationed patrol officers to be responsible for planning the boundaries of each Baojia in order to facilitate the election. Anyone with one of the following conditions is not allowed to be elected as town, Bao, or Jia head: (Zi) Those under the age of twenty years; (Chou) Those who have not resided in this port for three years and have no legitimate occupation; (Yin) Those with bad habits; (Mao) Those with unclear backgrounds; (Chen) Those with mental illness; (Ji) Those who are illiterate; (Wu) Those who have harmed the Republic of China or acted as local tyrants and bullies and have been sentenced; (Wei) Those who have been deprived of civil rights. (3) The organization of Baojia must be based on household registration, customs, terrain, and other special circumstances, and organized according to the following methods: (Zi) The organization of each household, Jia, and Bao should start from one side and organize adjacent houses in sequential order; (Chou) For the remaining households that do not make up a Jia, those with six or more households may form a separate Jia, and those with five or fewer households should be incorporated into a neighboring Jia. The same applies to the remaining Jia; (Yin) The investigation of temples within each district will be subject to separate regulations. The investigation of household registration shall be supervised by the chiefs of each Public Security Sub-bureau (and district heads). The procedure is as follows: (Zi) After the household registration is determined, the head should thoroughly implement the investigation together with the household heads to ensure that the organization matches the actual situation; (Chou) After each Bao is determined, the town head should implement a review together with the stationed patrol officer; (Yin) After each town is determined, the chief of the Public Security Sub-bureau (and district head) should conduct a serious review; (Mao) After each district is determined, the Bureau will send personnel to review with the town and Bao heads. (5) After the household registration is determined, Baojia doorplates will be issued separately and affixed to the upper end of the street door. They must not be lost or damaged. If there is any loss, report it to the town office for reissuance. The household registration of each household should be filled out truthfully at the same time, and there must be no concealment or false reporting. The investigation form should be personally imprinted by the household head of each household to ensure responsibility. (The doorplate style will be determined separately.) (6) Any increase, decrease, or change in the household must be reported immediately: household to Jia, Jia to Bao, Bao to town, town to the stationed police in their jurisdiction. The stationed police report the household change form to the district (i.e., Public Security Sub-bureau) on a monthly basis. The district then compiles the household change form within its jurisdiction and reports it to the General Bureau. However, the time from the household to the stationed police must not exceed forty-eight hours. (The reporting form will be ordered separately, and the reporting method will be specified when the meeting is convened.) (7) After the Baojia is determined, household registration may increase or decrease from time to time, and Baojia should be added or merged separately at the end of the year as required. (8) After the district and town heads are recommended, the Bureau will add an appointment and issue an official seal. After the Bao and Jia heads are recommended, they may be appointed by the district head. (9) If the district head finds that the town, Bao, or Jia head is incompetent or believes that a replacement is necessary, they may report to the Bureau for approval and re-election by the original recommender. However, if any town head has illegal behavior, or if the Jia head believes that the Bao head has illegal behavior, they may directly report to the Bureau in a joint name, and a re-election will be held after verification. (10) After the Baojia is determined, the district head should convene a Baojia meeting of town, Bao, and Jia heads together with the chief police officers and officers of the Public Security Sub-bureau to discuss and abide by the Baojia regulations. The regulations should be formulated on the following matters: (Zi) Matters concerning the functions and office locations of district, town, Bao, and Jia heads, as well as the names and order of each district, town, Bao, and Jia; (Chou) Matters concerning the compilation of doorplates and investigation of household registration; (Yin) Matters concerning the inspection and banning of people entering and leaving the territory; (Mao) Matters concerning water and fire rescue and alert; (Chen) Matters concerning the notification and search of bandit disasters; (Ji) Matters concerning the protection of highways, telephone poles, bridges, and all transportation; (Wu) Necessary matters concerning maintaining local security; (Wei) Matters concerning the date of convening meetings, the number of decisions, and the method of convening emergency meetings. (11) After the Baojia regulations are formulated, all district, town, Bao, and Jia heads should sign and report them to the Bureau for record. (12) The powers of the Jia, Bao, town, and district heads are as follows: (Zi) Jia head: 1. Responsible for maintaining the security and order within the Jia under the command and supervision of the Bao head; 2. Assist the Bao head in performing duties; 3. Investigate the household registration within the Jia, compile doorplates, and obtain joint security and joint liability undertakings; 4. Assist the police in searching for and arresting criminals; 5. Advise residents not to engage in illegal activities; 6. Inspect traitors and investigate the entry and exit of people. (Chou) Bao head: 1. The Bao head is responsible for maintaining local security under the command and supervision of the town head; 2. Supervise the Jia heads in performing their duties; 3. Assist the town head in performing their duties; 4. Advise residents not to engage in illegal activities; 5. Assist the police in searching for and arresting bandits; 6. Report bandits; 7. Other important matters concerning local security. (Yin) Town head: 1. The town head is responsible for maintaining local security; 2. Examine the diligence of the Bao and Jia heads; 3. Improve local relations and public security under the command of the district head; 4. Jointly inspect the household registration of each Baojia with the patrol officer to see if there are any omissions or concealments. (13) If each Baojia head discovers bandits, they should report it immediately and must not conceal it. Otherwise, they will be held jointly liable for colluding with bandits. If the residents find that each Baojia head has concealed bandits, they may report it jointly and have it investigated and handled, but there must be no acts of taking revenge or looking at faces. (14) Each household should jointly provide a joint security and joint liability undertaking with the households within the Baojia. The same applies to the town and Bao heads. (15) If residents within each Baojia have firearms, they should report to the Bureau for inspection, issue a license, brand them, and register them. Violators will be punished as illegally possessing military weapons. (16) In order to save expenses, the Bureau has decided that the district head will be concurrently held by the chief of each sub-bureau and will not be paid a separate public fee. The town head may set up a town office, and the Bureau will issue 10 yuan in office expenses per month, and the sub-bureau will allocate a capable police officer to assist the town head in handling clerical and communication matters. Each Baojia head will work at their home, but there is no public fee. (17) The term of office for district, town, Bao, and Jia heads is limited to one year. If they perform well, they may be reappointed. (18) Each district, town, Bao, and Jia head must be absolutely responsible for all matters in their respective areas and must not shirk responsibility or be absent arbitrarily when summoned. (19) Chahar Province is in a special position, and its district, town, Bao, and Jia heads must absolutely keep secrets when dealing with external matters. (20) If there are confidential matters that should not be announced, and the district, town, Bao, and Jia heads leak them, they will be punished according to the severity of the circumstances. (21) If each district, town, Bao, and Jia head fails to fulfill their responsibilities, they will be punished according to the severity of the circumstances. (22) If each district, town, Bao, and Jia head abuses their powers, accepts bribes, or delays important official duties, the district head may report to the Bureau according to the circumstances and punish them according to law. (23) If each town and Bao head encounters one of the following situations, the district head may report to the Bureau for separate rewards and punishments: (Zi) Those who detect the intention of bandits to invade and report it quickly, thus preserving the public security of the provincial capital; (Chou) Those who uncover important organs of bandits and other illegal elements, or who capture them due to reporting, and are interrogated and dealt with according to law; (Yin) Those who seize illegally hidden military weapons; (Mao) Those who assist the military and police in capturing bandits; (Chen) Those whose Baojia boundaries have accurate populations and who handle matters seriously. (24) The methods of reporting matters by each district, town, and Bao head are listed below: (Zi) If illegal or reactionary elements are detected within the boundary, they must be reported clearly and secretly according to the severity and urgency of the circumstances; (Chou) In the event of special emergencies, if there is any delay, which may lead to major changes, each town and Bao head may report directly to the Bureau or the district (face-to-face reports are also acceptable) in order to be agile and avoid delaying important official duties; (Yin) All personnel involved in confidential reporting should strictly keep secrets. If it is found that there is any leakage of confidential information, they will be severely punished. (25) If there are any matters not covered in these measures, they may be temporarily requested to be amended. (26) These measures shall be implemented from the date of approval. (30) Shop assistant Wang Peilin entered the shop at the age of sixteen as an apprentice and has been there for ten years. The relationship between guest and host is still fairly harmonious, but his nature is quite stingy and he is unwilling to be accommodating with money. He also does not issue year-end dividends. Disappointed, Wang could not help but hold a grudge. Guo had two sons and a daughter. The eldest son, Wenyu, is now six years old and attends Anduo Elementary School in Special District Three. He is intelligent and loved by his father. At 10:00 a.m. on November 29, Wenyu came to the shop from his residence and was seen by Wang, who suddenly had a murderous intent. Taking advantage of the unpreparedness, he lured him to the black room next to the Bankers Association’s ball field where new photo negatives were stored. He untied his white silk trouser belt and strangled Wenyu in the box in five minutes. He still locked the black room and calmly returned to the shop, upstairs to serve as usual. Guo did not see his son and asked the shop assistants, all of whom said they did not know. Wang said that he had seen two acquaintances take him away and even named the people to confirm it. Guo did not suspect anything. At 4:00 p.m. that afternoon, Wang went to a friend's banquet at Weiyu Villa in the French Concession. At 6:00 p.m., he even called Guo, saying that his son had been found, but he needed to prepare 5,000 yuan to redeem him. Only then did Guo realize that something was wrong, but he only suspected kidnapping and did not expect the tragedy. He reported the situation of kidnapping and extortion to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and detectives were sent out, but there was no effect. However, Wang seemed to be acting on impulse and had no plan. He had no money and could not go far. After the banquet at Weiyu, he crossed the river alone and wandered in the streets of Wuchang for a day and night. On the evening of the 30th, he still crossed the Han River and entered the Hailand Hotel on Jianghan Road. As soon as he opened the room, detectives arrived. When he crossed the river, detectives from the Public Security Bureau had been waiting on the Jianggan side with his photo, so it was not difficult to find him by picture. After Wang was arrested, he personally wrote a simple confession in the hotel, directly admitting that Wenyu had been strangled to death and hidden in a box in the dark room. He also admitted his outrageous behavior.

A Shocking Box Corpse Case Occurs in Hankou; Six-Year-Old Young Master of Qixin Photo Studio Tragically Strangled; Corpse Hidden in a Box, Extortion of Huge Sums by Phone; Murderer is a Young Shop Assistant Who Claims to Be Seeking Revenge 68

Hankou Correspondence: A shocking murder case recently occurred in Hankou. The murderer is a young shop assistant who used extremely cruel methods on the young master, who was only six years old. After hiding the body in a box, he even extorted huge sums of money from the shop owner by phone. After the Municipal Public Security Bureau mobilized urgently, the case was quickly solved. The bizarre case spread throughout Wuhan. Guo Zhiyi, a native of Wuxi, Jiangsu, opened the Qixin Photo Studio on Jianghan Road in Special District Three of Hankou City. He has been in business for ten years and has accumulated huge wealth. The studio employs many shop assistants, one of whom is responsible for repairing negatives and does not want to involve others. He also said that the great revenge has been avenged and he has no regrets even if he dies. Later, he was escorted to the General Bureau and talked eloquently and vividly. After hearing the news, Guo rushed to the black room and found Wenyu's body in the box. The strangulation marks on his neck were very deep, and blood was flowing from all seven orifices, which was unbearable to watch. The Hankou Local Court was dispatched to inspect the body and confirmed that he had been strangled to death before his death. Wang's confession at the Public Security Bureau was as follows: "The Qixin Photo Studio was originally formed by five or six shareholders. Shop assistants usually have dividends. Later, the shareholders withdrew, and Tong Zhiyi operated it independently. The business became increasingly prosperous, but Guo was stingy and did not distribute the dividends. My grandmother was seriously ill and urged me to return to my hometown. Guo initially refused to lend me travel expenses. After pleading, he only lent me fifty yuan and made me write two IOUs. When I came to Hankou from Wuxi, I unfortunately fell ill. Guo initially promised to give me one yuan for medical expenses, but after repeated requests, he gave me three yuan and often humiliated and ridiculed me, so I held a grudge. At 10:00 a.m. on the 29th, the young master came to the shop, so I led him to the empty room where Qixin Photo Enlargement was done and strangled him with my trouser belt. He died in five minutes. I still returned to the shop to work. At 4:00 p.m., I went to a banquet at Weiyu Restaurant. After the banquet, I spoke to the shop owner on the phone. I first asked if the young master had returned to the shop. He replied that he had not returned. I said that he might not be able to return home for two or three days and said that he should prepare 5,000 yuan. When he heard this, he was very anxious and told me to return to the shop immediately, otherwise he would report to the Garrison Headquarters. I ignored him and crossed the river. I asked him for money just to make him happy and had no other intentions. After arriving in Wuchang, I only wandered on the road. I returned to Hankou and was arrested at the Hailand Hotel because I had no money, so I couldn't escape." There are two suspicious points in this case: (1) Stinginess in issuing wages and not giving dividends is not a deep hatred, so why kill his son? (2) Since he killed his son, why notify him by phone, which is equivalent to admitting it himself, and dare to publicly travel back and forth to Wuhan? Therefore, there are other reasons to suspect the origin of the murderous intent. (December 2)

Songjiang: Business Community Requests Reduction in Electricity Fees 69

The local electricity company originally sold electricity at 25 cents per unit, and merchants already felt that the electricity charges were too high. They had previously discussed requesting a reduction, but at that time they were preparing to connect electricity to Shanghai, so they waited until the Songjiang-Shanghai electricity connection was completed. Now that Shanghai electricity has been transmitted, the business community believes that the local electricity price is too high and has asked the Chamber of Commerce to negotiate with the electricity company authorities. The County Chamber of Commerce held a joint meeting of executive and supervisory committees the other day to discuss the issue of reducing electricity fees. The meeting decided to convene various guilds on a regular basis and send a letter to the electricity company inviting them to attend and discuss the extent of the reduction. It also discussed the methods for our business community to express itself regarding bandit suppression and pacification, and notified various guilds and shops to collect one day's income from both labor and capital, with the capital side used to慰勞 the soldiers at the front and the labor side used for the frugality movement, with a deadline for submission to the Chamber of Commerce for separate forwarding. A one-day movement committee was also formed, with the executive and supervisory committee members of the Chamber of Commerce and the chairmen of various guilds as members, to provide guidance.

Wuxi: Continued Collection of Feast Tax 72

The local feast tax in Wuxi has been contracted by merchants through bidding by the county government and collected according to the quota, which has been included in the local regular budget. The contract period for the previous feast tax contractors in various rural areas expired at the end of October of this year. Starting from November, new contractors will be recruited, new contracts will be signed, donation tickets will be printed, and the collection will continue. Yesterday, the county government issued a notice ordering all restaurant owners and catering chefs to comply. In the future, all weddings, funerals, celebrations, sacrifices, and banquets should be taxed according to regulations and should not be delayed or evaded, lest they be punished.

Crazy Woman Sets Fire in Vain 73

Wu Er, a resident of Houxicao Village, He Township, Di Yi District, had a well-to-do family with a motorized boat. His wife, Wu Zhang, suffered from mental illness, which recurred from time to time. The other day, Wu went out to grind rice, and Zhang was guarding the door at home. Unexpectedly, her dementia broke out, and she set fire to the house, which spread to the neighbors. With the best efforts of the fire dragons, the fire was extinguished, but all of Wu's houses were turned into ashes, resulting in immeasurable donations and losses. Most regrettably, his family had more than 400 yuan in cash, which was also burned.

Expand Anti-Drug Propaganda 74

The Second District Commissioner's Office previously received telegrams from the Provincial Civil Affairs Department and the National Anti-Smoking Commissioner, stating that the anti-drug deadline had expired. Starting from the 26th year, anyone who manufactures, sells, or smokes drugs would be sentenced to death. However, there are still many ignorant people in various places who have not awakened and reformed. The propaganda work has not been able to penetrate into the folk and promote their awareness. Within the 25th year, the governments of all provinces, cities, and counties, as well as the anti-smoking committees, should unite with local party, government, military, academic, self-government organizations, various institutions, and impartial personages, districts, Baojia leaders, etc., to participate in the organization of a cleansing drug meeting to publicize as much as possible, and stipulate four methods: (1) Concise and awakening announcements and slogans; (2) Concise paintings; (3) Open-air gatherings, parades, and speeches; (4) Knocking on gongs to notify households. The above points should be handled uniformly in urban and rural towns, and completed and canceled by the end of the 25th year. Yesterday, a special telegram was sent to the governments of the eight counties under its jurisdiction: Wuxi, Wujin, Jiangyin, Wuxian, Wujiang, Kunshan, Taicang, and Changshu, urging them to comply and report by December 5th.

Suspension of Freight Transport on the Longhai Railway 75

This year, there is a bumper harvest in various places, and the products are very abundant. Wuxi is a district where grains and food are concentrated, and merchants from other ports have come to Wuxi to purchase them one after another. Most of them are from Shaanxi, Guanzhong, Henan, Luoyang, and Tianjin, Jinan. They are all loaded by the railway bureau, but there are not enough vehicles. Various rice, miscellaneous grains, cotton yarn, and cloth waiting for loading are piled up like mountains, and the goods stored in the station's freight yard are also extremely crowded. Dozens of heavy-laden freighters lined up along the river, waiting to negotiate with the station for trucks to load. However, yesterday, the Wuxi Station suddenly received a telegram from the Transportation Department, stating that all goods transported to various places on the Longhai Line, whether rice, flour, must be temporarily suspended. As a result, grain merchants and merchants in general were extremely anxious. There are currently more than 40,000 bags of grain and more than 20,000 bags of flour that are urgently needed to be transported, but there is no way.

Nantong: Ramifications of the Embezzlement of Stolen Money Case 78

The Commissioner's Office discovered stolen money in the Yuxi bandit robbery case of 15,000 yuan. Yao Dangping, the leader of the detective team, and Tan Wei Yang Weiting, etc., embezzled and embezzled it for their own benefit and have been sent to the court for interrogation and detention. It has now been further investigated that they had previously shot and killed an 11-year-old boy named Xu. Prosecutor Xu was sent to open the coffin to verify the facts and investigate the case thoroughly.

Yangzhou: Character Association Raises Clothes to Aid Suiyuan 79

The Jiangdu Red Cross Branch, believing that the Sui territory is extremely cold, with rain and snow flying, and the loyal and brave soldiers are fighting in the icy and snowy ground, suffering hardships, has sent a commissioner to solicit donations of winter clothing to aid the front. Today (1st), it has begun to convene members to discuss fundraising methods. After the planning is completed, it will send members to solicit donations.

Gaoyou: All Circles Enthusiastically Aid Suiyuan 80

All parts of the country are enthusiastically aiding Suiyuan. Since the founding of the Minde Society in this county, all circles have launched a vigorous movement to aid Suiyuan. The County Party Department convened various institutions and groups at 10:00 a.m. on the 30th to discuss the organization of a National Contribution One-Day Income Movement Promotion Committee. After being recommended by the County Party Department, County Government Chamber of Commerce, Property Office, Buddhist Association, First District Office, and Education Bureau, the seven institutions served as committee members. It was stipulated that work would begin on December 2nd. The County Chamber of Commerce also notified various institutions, groups, and guilds to initiate one-day income assistance to Suiyuan, and set December 4th to convene a Conference to Comfort Soldiers to Defend Suiyuan. In addition, the Nando Waimazhuang industry in this county initiated a donation of one day's income from various wheat farmers and transportation firms to the soldiers defending Suiyuan, and has collected 200 yuan, which will be remitted to the Shanghai Suiyuan Comforting and Protecting Soldiers Association within a few days. In addition to donating 23 yuan and 20 cents from all the staff and students, Chengnan Elementary School in this county organized a Suiyuan Fundraising Group to raise 157 yuan and 59 cents, totaling 180 yuan and 79 cents. It has been remitted by the Bank of Communications to this newspaper to comfort the soldiers at the front in Suiyuan.

Jiaxing: Sending Personnel to Take Over the Two Chambers of Commerce 81

After the Construction Department dispatched inspectors to the chambers of commerce in the two towns of Wangdian and Xinzhen, it was deemed that the organization was not sound, and the department ordered the county to abolish the chambers of commerce in the two towns and merge them into the County Chamber of Commerce to establish branch offices. After receiving the order, the County Chamber of Commerce has recommended Jiang Fuqing to take over the Wangdian Town Chamber of Commerce and Lu Chujue to take over the Xinzhen Town Chamber of Commerce. Feng Rixuan was appointed as the director of the Wangdian Branch Office and Gao Zhiqi was appointed as the director of the Xinzhen Branch Office. The County Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the County Government requesting them to send personnel to supervise the handover in order to show prudence.

Jiashan: Prisoners Go on Hunger Strike to Aid Suiyuan 82

Over two hundred male and female prisoners in the county prison and detention center jointly submitted a petition to the prison warden, Lin Tinghou, requesting to go on a one-day hunger strike. All the food expenses saved from that day would be donated to support the soldiers in Suiyuan. At the same time, considering the urgency of the national crisis, they specifically telegraphed the entire country, pleading for a general amnesty so that they could atone for their crimes by sacrificing their lives for the country.

Ningbo: County Magistrate of Tai County Encounters Bandits During Inspection Tour 83

Cao Zhonglin, the magistrate of Fenghua County, along with official Guan Zhongyi and two police officers, took a sea-route automobile to Fangmen on the 30th to inspect the coastal areas. They stayed overnight in Lengxikeng. The next day, they went to Xiachen and other places for inspection. After staying overnight, they proceeded to Wujiabu and . Unexpectedly, near Maochi, they suddenly encountered a bandit in luxurious clothes. The magistrate, finding the bandit's behavior suspicious, ordered him to stop. The bandit reached into his pockets. The magistrate, knowing he was dealing with a bandit, immediately drew his pistol and fired it into the air. At the same time, the official and the two policemen raised their wooden s and aimed at the bandit. Seeing he was outnumbered, the bandit fled. Cao and his group chased him to Maochi, but the bandit was gone. They saw one person fertilizing a field and another cutting firewood by the roadside. When questioned, both were evasive. Since the bandit had passed by them, Cao suspected them of harboring the bandit. He ordered the local militia to escort them to the county for interrogation.

Vicious Woman Gouges Out Husband's Eyes 84

A farmer surnamed Lu from Luojiang, Cinan, married a woman named Ying. She was extremely fierce and had an affair. Because her husband, though foolish as an ox, could not openly be aware, and do as she pleased, in the afternoon of the first day of this month, Ying took advantage of her husband's afternoon nap and, with a sharp pair of scissors, gouged out his eyes. Lu, in extreme pain, screamed for help. Neighbors rushed over upon hearing the cries and, seeing the situation, berated Ying for her cruelty and ordered her to provide medical treatment and support her husband forever. Seeing that the public's anger was overwhelming, Ying agreed to the conditions and pleaded for the matter not to be pursued further, thus settling the matter.

Hangzhou: Station Master Found Embezzling 85

Chen Xuelou, the deputy station master of Mingguang Station on the Jinpu Railway, fled to Hangzhou to hide under the alias Gong Maoru, residing at No. 8, Renhe Road, Xinshi Market, due to his involvement in embezzlement with the station master, Song Yanwu. He was apprehended yesterday by the Public Security Bureau and sent to the Hangzhou District Court for trial. Chen refused to confess, so the court ordered a deposit of 1,000 yuan for bail, but he could not secure it. He was then placed in custody by the detention center, and the Jinpu Railway Bureau was notified for investigation.

Local News

River Rice Confiscated, Source Cut Off: Shanghai Northern Rice Merchants Temporarily Suspend Market; All Remaining Stocks Sold Off Yesterday; Representatives from Various Counties Arrive in Shanghai to Discuss Solutions 86

According to Dagongshe, after the Shanghai Municipal Government learned that Jiading County had confiscated rice boats passing through the area, causing panic among Shanghai residents regarding their food supply, it telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday, requesting their immediate release. Representatives from Shanghai's rice industry associations are engaging in negotiations. The northern part of Shanghai has suspended rice trading due to the interruption of river rice supplies. Details are as follows:

Representatives Petition

Members of the Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Association, Qiang Zisheng and Fu Qiangeng; members of the Shanghai Rice Merchants Association, Jiang Shizhi; and director of the Changshu Guild, Shi Zufu, went to the Municipal Government and the Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday morning to petition. They requested that the Jiangsu Provincial Government be telegraphed to order the Jiading County Government to release the detained rice boats from various counties, such as Xichangchang and Kun, at the Jiwang Temple area, to maintain the food supply for Shanghai residents. The representatives then, at 5 p.m., carried a letter of introduction from the Bureau of Social Affairs and went to the Jiading County Government to meet County Magistrate Guo Yaofeng, requesting their immediate release. Magistrate Guo expressed earnestly that he greatly valued the food supply for Shanghai residents, but was bound by provincial orders and had to await a reply from the province before releasing them.

Telegraph to Jiangsu for Release

After receiving the reports and requests from the petitioning representatives of the rice industry associations yesterday morning, the Municipal Government telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Government, requesting the immediate release of the rice boats detained in Jiading County. Pan Gongzhan, the director of the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, also telegraphed Yu Jingtang, the director of the Jiangsu Department of Civil Affairs, requesting him to follow the domestic food circulation measures passed by the Executive Yuan and order the Jiading County Government to release the boats immediately to maintain the food supply for Shanghai residents. At the same time, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, local coordination associations, and other organizations also sent telegrams to the Jiangsu provincial authorities.

Northern Shanghai Market Suspended

Currently, over 180 rice boats have been detained in the Jiwang Temple area of Wusong Port, causing navigation to be blocked. The northern Shanghai rice market has suspended trading because the original river rice supply has been cut off and the source is being confiscated, causing rice prices to rise by another 20-30 cents yesterday. Since the river rice was unloaded at the close of the market at 3 p.m. yesterday, there is no way to trade this morning, so it is necessary to temporarily suspend the market.

Various Counties Arrive in Shanghai

Since the Jiading County Jiwang Temple confiscated a large number of rice boats, merchants from various inland counties are extremely panicked. To investigate the truth about the confiscated rice boats, rice industry associations from Wuxi, Changshu, Suzhou, Wujiang, Kunshan, and other counties have sent representatives to Shanghai to discuss countermeasures with Shanghai's rice industry organizations.

Minister Kong's Health is Unwell: Did Not Go to the Central Bank Yesterday 87

A reporter from the Central News Agency went to the Central Bank yesterday on business, intending to meet with Vice President Kong, but he was not there. Upon inquiring with a secretary, it was learned that Minister Kong had previously taken leave to treat his heart disease. According to the doctor, he should have taken a longer period of rest, but Kong felt that his responsibilities were too great and did not want to harm the public interest for personal gain. Even during his treatment, he continued to handle important affairs of the Ministry of Finance and the Central Bank while leaning on his bed. Two weeks ago, feeling that the national crisis was serious and his personal responsibilities were even greater, he disobeyed the doctor's orders and went out to the Central Bank to work every day despite his illness. He originally planned to go to the capital soon, but the doctor insisted that his heart condition would be aggravated by the vibrations of the train, so it did not happen. Yesterday morning (the 2nd), he went to the bank as usual and was about to summon his staff to handle official business when he suddenly felt dizzy and had chills all over his body. He hurried back to his residence to call a doctor, who said that his original illness had not recovered and was compounded by a cold. After taking medication, his fever gradually subsided this morning (the 3rd). He is avoiding wind as per the doctor's orders, so he did not go to work yesterday.

Huang Fu's Condition: Fainted Once Yesterday Afternoon 88

According to the Central News Agency, Huang Fu, a member of the National Government, fainted once yesterday afternoon. After careful diagnosis and treatment by traditional Chinese doctors Fan Shisheng and Liu Zhengyu, he woke up immediately. His condition improved afterward, and he was even able to sleep peacefully at night. His friends Xu Qingfu, Xu Xiuzhi, and Shen Yi visited him and were relieved to see that Huang's condition had improved slightly. However, his condition is still in a critical stage, and whether he can be saved depends on whether there are any changes within the next three days. The report from the Japanese Domei News Agency last night that Huang had died of illness at his residence at 2:30 p.m. on the third is completely inaccurate. Dr. Fan Shisheng has denied it.

The Farmers Bank of China Manages Agricultural Warehouse Loans in Fujian Province: Totaling 2 Million, Monthly Interest Rate of 8%; Discounting and Remittance Services are Handled by the Bank 89

The Farmers Bank of China has been expanding its agricultural loans to various provinces in recent years as much as possible. It has now established a 2 million yuan agricultural warehouse collateral loan fund with the Fujian Provincial Rural Cooperative Committee, and lending has already begun. Details are as follows:

Term and Purpose

The purpose and term of the agricultural warehouse loans are stipulated as follows: (1) Construction or repair of warehouse buildings shall not exceed 60% of the total cost of materials and labor and shall be repaid in installments within three years. (2) Purchase of processing equipment shall not exceed 70% of the total cost and shall be repaid in installments within three years. (3) Collateral warehousing is limited to 70% of the market value of the collateral, but shall not exceed 40 yuan per person and shall be repaid within ten months. (4) Business operations are to be determined on a temporary basis and shall be repaid within six months. (5) The total amount of the agricultural warehouse collateral fund is temporarily set at 2 million yuan, with 70% of the actual market value of the collateral lent out, using the agricultural products stored in each warehouse as collateral. (6) The interest rate on agricultural warehouse loans is temporarily set at 8% per month, and the collateral period is limited to a maximum of ten months.

Scope of Loans

The scope of agricultural warehouse collateral loans is stipulated to include the following 34 counties: Minhou, Longxi, Fuqing, Fuan, Minqing, Lianjiang, Luoyuan, Ningde, Changle, Pingtan, Jian'ou, Nanping, Pucheng, Putian, Jinjiang, Xianyou, Longyan, Shaxian, Changting, Tongan, Dehua, Zhangpu, Dongshan, Shanghang, Liancheng, Ninghua, Yong'an, Jiangle, Taining, Jianning, Shaowu, Jianyang, Shunchang, and Chong'an. The Farmers Bank of China may send personnel to investigate the content of agricultural warehouses in the above locations at any time, audit accounts, and assist in the operation of agricultural warehouses. At the same time, all agricultural warehouses must be insured against fire, and the insurance policy must be handed over to the Farmers Bank of China for safekeeping. All discounting, remittance, and collateral services of agricultural warehouses shall be handled by the Farmers Bank of China.

Ding Peilai Discusses Sino-Japanese Relations 91

According to the Continental Daily, when the Shanghai Youth Club held a luncheon at the American Club yesterday afternoon (the 2nd), Ding Peilai, the correspondent for the British Manchester Guardian and various important American publications, spoke about the important changes in Sino-Japanese relations in the past year, stating briefly that the situation between China and Japan had undergone significant changes in the past year for various reasons. One of the reasons for the change in Japan's policy towards China was the victory of President Chiang in resolving the Southwest dispute. This move not only greatly boosted the morale of the Chinese people but also eliminated the risk of internal divisions in the event of war with Japan. The military strength of the central government has greatly increased as a result, allowing it to cope with Japanese aggression. For this reason, Foreign Minister Zhang Qun was able to respond to the formidable demands made by Japanese Ambassador Kawagoe in October with a number of counter-demands. This is the first time since 1931 that China has dared to confront Japan. President Chiang recently held multiple meetings with northern leaders such as Han Fuju and Yan Xishan, and their opinions were in agreement. The central government also participated in the defense of Suiyuan to resist the mixed forces of Mongols and bandits, seemingly aided by Japan. This is also clear evidence of China's increasing internal unity. During this period, the central government's finances also became more stable, and military funding increased daily. The above points are indeed of great significance to the overall situation, but Japan's moderate attitude towards several major incidents between China and Japan is not entirely due to this. At the end of this autumn, a total of five Japanese residents were killed and four were injured in various places in China. In the past, any one of these incidents would have been enough for the Japanese to take the opportunity to implement severe actions under the pretext. The reason why Japan has been restrained is that while China's internal strength is increasing, Japan's internal situation is deteriorating. Ding then cited facts to draw the audience's attention to the exposure of Japan's domestic weaknesses in February of this year, saying that the real key to this matter lies in the serious difficulties Japan is encountering in its political, economic, and social aspects. After detailing the historical background of these weaknesses, Ding went on to discuss Japan's financial difficulties, saying that by the end of 1936, Japan's total debt was several times greater than it had been five years earlier. The national debt borne by each Japanese citizen was previously lower than that borne by the people of Britain, France, and the United States, but now it is increasing by 1 billion yen per year, which is shocking to hear. If the military had not moderated its financial demands, the trend would have continued to increase, but the military's attitude is tough, and it seems unlikely that it will be willing to do so at present. Ding then went on to describe the large increase in military spending in Japan's budget, saying that the authorities are about to levy new taxes to make up for this sharp increase in expenditure. Finance Minister Baba has proposed a financial reform plan aimed at complying with the military's demands, but the public strongly opposes it because it will increase their burden. The business community is also very disapproving. Japan's massive increase in military buildup is actually due to fear of Soviet Russia. Since 1931, the Red Army in eastern Siberia has increased from six divisions to about 250,000 men, and their combat equipment is complete, including long-range bombers that can threaten Japan's major industrial areas. The large increase in Soviet military strength is sufficient to affect Japan's position in China. All Japanese leaders know that if Soviet Russia continues to develop its Far Eastern military strength, Japan will find it difficult to implement its development policy on the Asian continent, and they fear that their position in Manchuria will also be threatened. Furthermore, Japan is gradually realizing that pacifying Manchuria is not easy. Since 1931, Japan has spent 1 billion yen in Manchuria. During this period, no fewer than 5,000 Japanese soldiers have died, and another 200,000 have either been injured or have returned home from Manchuria due to illness. Ding finally touched on the expansion of China's internal strength, saying that its state makes it difficult for Japan to act rashly in North China. The Western powers, especially Great Britain, are now concerned about China's affairs, which is sufficient to overturn some of Japan's assumptions and disappoint it.
